{\footnotesize template$<$class T, class = std\+::enable\+\_\+if\+\_\+t$<$std\+::is\+\_\+pointer$<$\+T$>$\+::value$>$$>$ }\\using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacekiwi_a4091a6e55c2adb06034f8816c093ab88}{Owner}} = T
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespacekiwi_a4091a6e55c2adb06034f8816c093ab88}{Owner}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}T\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} is designed as a safety mechanism for code that must deal directly with raw pointers that own memory. Ideally such code should be restricted to the implementation of low-\/level abstractions. {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespacekiwi_a4091a6e55c2adb06034f8816c093ab88}{Owner}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}T\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} can also be used as a stepping point in converting legacy code to use more modern RAII constructs, such as smart pointers. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
{\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time}{Time}} represents an absolute point in coordinated universal time (UTC), internally represented as microseconds (s/1,000,000) since the Windows epoch (1601-\/01-\/01 00\+:00\+:00 UTC). System-\/dependent clock interface routines are defined in time\+\_\+\+PLATFORM.\+cc. Note that values for {\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time}{Time}} may skew and jump around as the operating system makes adjustments to synchronize (e.\+g., with NTP servers). Thus, client code that uses the {\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time}{Time}} class must account for this.

{\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time_delta}{Time\+Delta}} represents a duration of time, internally represented in microseconds.

{\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time_ticks}{Time\+Ticks}} and {\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_thread_ticks}{Thread\+Ticks}} represent an abstract time that is most of the time incrementing, for use in measuring time durations. Internally, they are represented in microseconds. They cannot be converted to a human-\/readable time, but are guaranteed not to decrease (unlike the {\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time}{Time}} class). Note that {\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time_ticks}{Time\+Ticks}} may "{}stand still"{} (e.\+g., if the computer is suspended), and {\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_thread_ticks}{Thread\+Ticks}} will "{}stand still"{} whenever the thread has been de-\/scheduled by the operating system.

All time classes are copyable, assignable, and occupy 64 bits per instance. Prefer to pass them by value, e.\+g.\+:

void My\+Function(\+Time\+Delta arg);

All time classes support {\ttfamily operator\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}} with logging streams, e.\+g. {\ttfamily LOG(\+INFO)}. For human-\/readable formatting, use //base/i18n/time\+\_\+formatting.h.

Example use cases for different time classes\+:

\doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time}{Time}\+: Interpreting the wall-\/clock time provided by a remote system. Detecting whether cached resources have expired. Providing the user with a display of the current date and time. Determining the amount of time between events across re-\/boots of the machine.

\doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time_ticks}{Time\+Ticks}\+: Tracking the amount of time a task runs. Executing delayed tasks at the right time. Computing presentation timestamps. Synchronizing audio and video using \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time_ticks}{Time\+Ticks} as a common reference clock (lip-\/sync). Measuring network round-\/trip latency.

\doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_thread_ticks}{Thread\+Ticks}\+: Benchmarking how long the current thread has been doing actual work.

Serialization\+:

Use the helpers in //base/json/values\+\_\+util.h when serializing {\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time}{Time}} or {\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time_delta}{Time\+Delta}} to/from {\ttfamily base\+::\+Value}.

Otherwise\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time}{Time}\+: use {\ttfamily From\+Delta\+Since\+Windows\+Epoch()}/{\ttfamily To\+Delta\+Since\+Windows\+Epoch()}.
\item \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time_delta}{Time\+Delta}\+: use {\ttfamily base\+::\+Microseconds()}/{\ttfamily In\+Microseconds()}.
\end{DoxyItemize}

{\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_time_ticks}{Time\+Ticks}} and {\ttfamily \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_thread_ticks}{Thread\+Ticks}} do not have a stable origin; serialization for the purpose of persistence is not supported.

This contains stripped-\/down workalikes of some Boost classes\+:

iterator\+\_\+adaptor iterator\+\_\+facade

Rationale\+: the boost headers providing those classes are surprisingly large. The bloat comes from the headers themselves, but more so, their transitive includes.

These implementations are simple and minimal. They may be missing features provided by the Boost classes mentioned above. Also at this time they only support forward-\/iterators. They provide just enough for the few uses within Folly libs; more features will be slapped in here if and when they\textquotesingle{}re needed.

These classes may possibly add features as well. Care is taken not to change functionality where it\textquotesingle{}s expected to be the same (e.\+g. {\ttfamily dereference} will do the same thing).

These are currently only intended for use within Folly, hence their living under detail. Use outside Folly is not recommended.

To see how to use these classes, find the instances where this is used within Folly libs. Common use cases can also be found in {\ttfamily Iterators\+Test.\+cpp}.

This file defines platform-\/independent types for dealing with platform-\/dependent files. If possible, use the higher-\/level \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_file}{kiwi\+::\+File} class rather than these primitives.

Checks the requirements that the Hasher class must satisfy in order to be used with the standard library containers, for example {\ttfamily std\+::unordered\+\_\+set\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}T, Hasher\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}}. \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_a4091a6e55c2adb06034f8816c093ab88}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!Owner@{Owner}}
\index{Owner@{Owner}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Owner}{Owner}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_a4091a6e55c2adb06034f8816c093ab88} 
template$<$class T, class = std\+::enable\+\_\+if\+\_\+t$<$std\+::is\+\_\+pointer$<$\+T$>$\+::value$>$$>$ \\
using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacekiwi_a4091a6e55c2adb06034f8816c093ab88}{kiwi\+::\+Owner}} = T}



{\ttfamily \doxylink{namespacekiwi_a4091a6e55c2adb06034f8816c093ab88}{Owner}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}T\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} is designed as a safety mechanism for code that must deal directly with raw pointers that own memory. Ideally such code should be restricted to the implementation of low-\/level abstractions. {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespacekiwi_a4091a6e55c2adb06034f8816c093ab88}{Owner}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}T\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}} can also be used as a stepping point in converting legacy code to use more modern RAII constructs, such as smart pointers. 


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Must be a pointer type. And disallow construction from any type other than pointer type \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

enum class \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacekiwi_a7df83edab5560ff28ed4ebc60cebed70}{kiwi\+::\+Acquire\+Mallocated\+String}}\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [strong]}}

Defines a special acquisition method for constructing fbstring objects. \doxylink{namespacekiwi_a7df83edab5560ff28ed4ebc60cebed70}{Acquire\+Mallocated\+String} means that the user passes a pointer to a malloc-\/allocated string that the fbstring object will take into custody.

BASE\+\_\+\+EXPORT int64\+\_\+t kiwi\+::\+Compute\+Directory\+Size (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1_file_path}{File\+Path}} \&}]{root\+\_\+path}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Returns the total number of bytes used by all the files under {\ttfamily root\+\_\+path}.

This function is implemented using the \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_file_enumerator}{File\+Enumerator} class so it is not particularly speedy on any platform.

\Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_a60a5cfa5df6cc93c3804817084f57052}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!const\_cast\_function@{const\_cast\_function}}
\index{const\_cast\_function@{const\_cast\_function}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{const\_cast\_function()}{const\_cast\_function()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_a60a5cfa5df6cc93c3804817084f57052} 
template$<$typename Return\+Type, typename... Args$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1_function}{Function}}$<$ Return\+Type(Args...) const $>$ kiwi\+::const\+\_\+cast\+\_\+function (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1_function}{Function}}$<$ Return\+Type(Args...)$>$ \&\&}]{that}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [noexcept]}}

Casts a {\ttfamily \doxylink{classfolly_1_1_function}{folly\+::\+Function}} from non-\/const to a const signature.

NOTE\+: The name of {\ttfamily const\+\_\+cast\+\_\+function} should warn you that something potentially dangerous is happening. As a matter of fact, using {\ttfamily std\+::function} always involves this potentially dangerous aspect, which is why it is not considered fully const-\/safe or even const-\/correct. However, in most of the cases you will not need the dangerous aspect at all. Either you do not require invocation of the function from a const context, in which case you do not need to use {\ttfamily const\+\_\+cast\+\_\+function} and just use a non-\/const {\ttfamily \doxylink{classfolly_1_1_function}{folly\+::\+Function}}. Or, you may need invocation from const, but the callable you are wrapping does not mutate its state (e.\+g. it is a class object and implements {\ttfamily operator() const}, or it is a normal, non-\/mutable lambda), in which case you can wrap the callable in a const {\ttfamily \doxylink{classfolly_1_1_function}{folly\+::\+Function}} directly, without using {\ttfamily const\+\_\+cast\+\_\+function}. Only if you require invocation from a const context of a callable that may mutate itself when invoked you have to go through the above procedure. However, in that case what you do is potentially dangerous and requires the equivalent of a {\ttfamily const\+\_\+cast}, hence you need to call {\ttfamily const\+\_\+cast\+\_\+function}.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em that} & a non-\/const \doxylink{classfolly_1_1_function}{folly\+::\+Function}. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_af0d9ea63159f8a9f92646fcae1bf3956}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!copy@{copy}}
\index{copy@{copy}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{copy()}{copy()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_af0d9ea63159f8a9f92646fcae1bf3956} 
template$<$typename T$>$ \\
detail\+::decay\+\_\+t$<$ T $>$ kiwi\+::copy (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{T \&\&}]{value}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [constexpr]}, {\ttfamily [noexcept]}}

copy

Usable when you have a function with two overloads\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}class MyData;
void something(MyData&&);
void something(const MyData&);
\end{DoxyVerb}


Where the purpose is to make copies and moves explicit without having to spell out the full type names -\/ in this case, for copies, to invoke copy constructors.

When the caller wants to pass a copy of an lvalue, the caller may\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}void foo() {
  MyData data;
  something(folly::copy(data)); // explicit copy
  something(std::move(data)); // explicit move
  something(data); // const& - neither move nor copy
}
\end{DoxyVerb}


Note\+: If passed an rvalue, invokes the move-\/ctor, not the copy-\/ctor. This can be used to to force a move, where just using std\+::move would not\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}folly::copy(std::move(data)); // force-move, not just a cast to &&
\end{DoxyVerb}


Note\+: The following text appears in the standard\+: \begin{DoxyVerb}In several places in this Clause the operation //DECAY_COPY(x)// is
used. All such uses mean call the function `decay_copy(x)` and use the
result, where `decay_copy` is defined as follows:

  template <class T> decay_t<T> decay_copy(T&& v)
    { return std::forward<T>(v); }

http://www.open-std.org/jtc1/sc22/wg21/docs/papers/2014/n4296.pdf
  30.2.6 `decay_copy` [thread.decaycopy].
\end{DoxyVerb}


We mimic it, with a {\ttfamily noexcept} specifier for good measure. \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_ae379daf00c748739813e37270e578dd3}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!Crc32@{Crc32}}
\index{Crc32@{Crc32}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Crc32()}{Crc32()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_ae379daf00c748739813e37270e578dd3} 
BASE\+\_\+\+EXPORT uint32\+\_\+t kiwi\+::\+Crc32 (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{sum}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1span}{span}}$<$ const uint8\+\_\+t $>$}]{data}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

We generate the CRC-\/32 using the low order bits to select whether to XOR in the reversed polynomial 0x\+EDB88320. This is nice and simple, and allows us to keep the quotient in a uint32\+\_\+t. Since we\textquotesingle{}re not concerned about the nature of corruptions (i.\+e., we don\textquotesingle{}t care about bit sequencing, since we are handling memory changes, which are more grotesque) so we don\textquotesingle{}t bother to get the CRC correct for big-\/endian vs little-\/ending calculations. All we need is a nice hash, that tends to depend on all the bits of the sample, with very little chance of changes in one place impacting changes in another place.

This provides a simple, fast CRC-\/32 calculation that can be used for checking the integrity of data. It is not a "{}secure"{} calculation! {\ttfamily sum} can start with any seed or be used to continue an operation began with previous data. \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_af36300507ade71d4184c22720143fb71}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!CreateTemporaryFile@{CreateTemporaryFile}}
\index{CreateTemporaryFile@{CreateTemporaryFile}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{CreateTemporaryFile()}{CreateTemporaryFile()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_af36300507ade71d4184c22720143fb71} 
BASE\+\_\+\+EXPORT bool kiwi\+::\+Create\+Temporary\+File (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1_file_path}{File\+Path}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{path}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Creates a temporary file. The file will be empty and all handles closed after this function returns. The caller is responsible for deleting the file {\ttfamily path} points to, if appropriate.

\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
true if the temporary file was successfully created; false otherwise. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_a724068dd3390a2442ca488909f68ed72} 
BASE\+\_\+\+EXPORT bool kiwi\+::\+Delete\+File (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1_file_path}{File\+Path}} \&}]{path}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Deletes the given path, whether it\textquotesingle{}s a file or a directory. If it\textquotesingle{}s a directory, it\textquotesingle{}s perfectly happy to delete all of the directory\textquotesingle{}s contents, but it will not recursively delete subdirectories and their contents. Returns true if successful, false otherwise. It is considered successful to attempt to delete a file that does not exist.

In POSIX environment and if {\ttfamily path} is a symbolic link, this deletes only the symlink. (even if the symlink points to a non-\/existent file)

Deletes the given path, whether it\textquotesingle{}s a file or a directory. If it\textquotesingle{}s a directory, it\textquotesingle{}s perfectly happy to delete all of the directory\textquotesingle{}s contents, including subdirectories and their contents. Returns true if successful, false otherwise. It is considered successful to attempt to delete a file that does not exist.

In POSIX environment and if {\ttfamily path} is a symbolic link, this deletes only the symlink. (even if the symlink points to a non-\/existent file)

WARNING\+: USING THIS EQUIVALENT TO "{}rm -\/rf"{}, SO USE WITH CAUTION. \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_a0f08f6f93fa42280d07db0f3c4723df7}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!make\_scope\_exit@{make\_scope\_exit}}

template$<$typename Callable$>$ \\

Interface is specified by p0052r2. \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_a4b01fc85d65b8cda86e753f4a00ccb5f}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!MakeAbsoluteFilePath@{MakeAbsoluteFilePath}}
\index{MakeAbsoluteFilePath@{MakeAbsoluteFilePath}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{MakeAbsoluteFilePath()}{MakeAbsoluteFilePath()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_a4b01fc85d65b8cda86e753f4a00ccb5f} 
BASE\+\_\+\+EXPORT \mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1_file_path}{File\+Path}} kiwi\+::\+Make\+Absolute\+File\+Path (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1_file_path}{File\+Path}} \&}]{input}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

char\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} realpath(const char \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}restrict file\+\_\+name, char \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}restrict resolved\+\_\+name)

The realpath() function resolves all symbolic links, extra "{}/"{} characters, and references to /./ and /../ in file\+\_\+name. If the resolved\+\_\+name argument is non-\/\+NULL, the resulting absolute pathname is copied there (it must refer to a buffer capable of storing at least PATH\+\_\+\+MAX characters).

As a permitted extension to the standard, if resolved\+\_\+name is NULL, memory is allocated for the resulting absolute pathname, and is returned by realpath(). This memory should be freed by a call to free(3) when no longer needed.

The realpath() function will resolve both absolute and relative paths and return the absolute pathname corresponding to file\+\_\+name. All components of file\+\_\+name must exist when realpath() is called. Returns an absolute version of a relative path. Returns an empty path on error. This function can result in I/O so it can be slow.

On POSIX, this function calls realpath(), so\+: 1) it fails if the path does not exist. 2) it expands all symlink components of the path. 3) it removes "{}."{} and "{}.."{} directory components.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em input} & The input path, which can be relative or absolute. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_file_path}{File\+Path} representing the absolute (canonicalized) version of the input. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

bool kiwi\+::operator== (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1_dense_map_base}{Dense\+Map\+Base}}$<$ DerivedT, KeyT, ValueT, Key\+InfoT, BucketT $>$ \&}]{LHS}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classkiwi_1_1_dense_map_base}{Dense\+Map\+Base}}$<$ DerivedT, KeyT, ValueT, Key\+InfoT, BucketT $>$ \&}]{RHS}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Equality comparison for \doxylink{classkiwi_1_1_dense_map}{Dense\+Map}.

Iterates over elements of LHS confirming that each (key, value) pair in LHS is also in RHS, and that no additional pairs are in RHS. Equivalent to N calls to RHS.\+find and N value comparisons. Amortized complexity is linear, worst case is O(\+N\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}2) (if every hash collides). \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_a9825413f55ac9daa706ba13abb7ad6b8}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!strip\_ascii\_whitespace@{strip\_ascii\_whitespace}}

Terminates as if by forwarding to throw\+\_\+exception but in a noexcept context. \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_a1b0531b9bf4f9470756d9958881b8b8c}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!throw\_exception@{throw\_exception}}
\index{throw\_exception@{throw\_exception}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{throw\_exception()}{throw\_exception()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_a1b0531b9bf4f9470756d9958881b8b8c} 
template$<$typename Ex, typename... Args$>$ \\
KIWI\+\_\+\+ERASE void kiwi\+::throw\+\_\+exception (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Args \&\&...}]{args}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

throw\+\_\+exception

Construct and throw an exception if exceptions are enabled, or terminate if compiled with -\/fno-\/exceptions.

Does not perfectly forward all its arguments. Instead, in the interest of minimizing common-\/case inline code size, decays its arguments as follows\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item refs to arrays of char const are decayed to char const\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}
\item refs to arrays are otherwise invalid
\item refs to trivial types are decayed to values
\end{DoxyItemize}

The reason for treating refs to arrays as invalid is to avoid having two behaviors for refs to arrays, one for the general case and one for where the inner type is char const. Having two behaviors can be surprising, so avoid. \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_abe3cc88b10ffe4cc4b1796c4bf782900}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!throw\_exception@{throw\_exception}}
\index{throw\_exception@{throw\_exception}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{throw\_exception()}{throw\_exception()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_abe3cc88b10ffe4cc4b1796c4bf782900} 
template$<$typename Ex$>$ \\
KIWI\+\_\+\+NOINLINE void kiwi\+::throw\+\_\+exception (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Ex \&\&}]{ex}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

throw\+\_\+exception

Throw an exception if exceptions are enabled, or terminate if compiled with -\/fno-\/exceptions.

\Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_a6c19e808322b20a2c60d3e99bd308c3c}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!kHardwareConstructiveInterferenceSize@{kHardwareConstructiveInterferenceSize}}
\index{kHardwareConstructiveInterferenceSize@{kHardwareConstructiveInterferenceSize}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{kHardwareConstructiveInterferenceSize}{kHardwareConstructiveInterferenceSize}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_a6c19e808322b20a2c60d3e99bd308c3c} 
std\+::size\+\_\+t kiwi\+::k\+Hardware\+Constructive\+Interference\+Size = 64\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [constexpr]}}

Memory locations within the same cache line are subject to constructive interference, also known as true sharing, which is when accesses to some memory locations induce all memory locations within the same cache line to be cached, benefiting subsequent accesses to different memory locations within the same cache line and heping performance.

mimic\+: std\+::hardware\+\_\+constructive\+\_\+interference\+\_\+size, C++17 \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_ab62e9348a9aa9fee4c3ad6e41b995c61}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!kHardwareDestructiveInterferenceSize@{kHardwareDestructiveInterferenceSize}}
\index{kHardwareDestructiveInterferenceSize@{kHardwareDestructiveInterferenceSize}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{kHardwareDestructiveInterferenceSize}{kHardwareDestructiveInterferenceSize}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_ab62e9348a9aa9fee4c3ad6e41b995c61} 
std\+::size\+\_\+t kiwi\+::k\+Hardware\+Destructive\+Interference\+Size = 128\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [constexpr]}}

Memory locations within the same cache line are subject to destructive interference, also known as false sharing, which is when concurrent accesses to these different memory locations from different cores, where at least one of the concurrent accesses is or involves a store operation, induce contention and harm performance.

Microbenchmarks indicate that pairs of cache lines also see destructive interference under heavy use of atomic operations, as observed for atomic increment on Sandy Bridge.

We assume a cache line size of 64, so we use a cache line pair size of 128 to avoid destructive interference.

mimic\+: std\+::hardware\+\_\+destructive\+\_\+interference\+\_\+size, C++17 \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_a6e27a3836ba7f1fac20061739130f62d}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!kMaxAlign@{kMaxAlign}}
\index{kMaxAlign@{kMaxAlign}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{kMaxAlign}{kMaxAlign}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_a6e27a3836ba7f1fac20061739130f62d} 
std\+::size\+\_\+t kiwi\+::k\+Max\+Align = detail\+::max\+\_\+align\+\_\+v\+\_\+\+::value()\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [constexpr]}}

max\+\_\+align\+\_\+t is a type which is aligned at least as strictly as the most-\/aligned basic type (see the specification of std\+::max\+\_\+align\+\_\+t). This implementation exists because 32-\/bit i\+OS platforms have a broken std\+::max\+\_\+align\+\_\+t (see below).

You should refer to this as {\ttfamily \+::kiwi\+::max\+\_\+align\+\_\+t} in portable code, even if you have {\ttfamily using namespace kiwi;} because C11 defines a global namespace {\ttfamily max\+\_\+align\+\_\+t} type.

To be certain, we consider every non-\/void fundamental type specified by the standard. On most platforms {\ttfamily long double} would be enough, but i\+OS 32-\/bit has an 8-\/byte aligned {\ttfamily double} and {\ttfamily long long int} and a 4-\/byte aligned {\ttfamily long double}.

So far we\textquotesingle{}ve covered locals and other non-\/allocated storage, but we also need confidence that allocated storage from {\ttfamily malloc}, {\ttfamily new}, etc will also be suitable for objects with this alignment requirement.

Apple document that their implementation of malloc will issue 16-\/byte granularity chunks for small allocations (large allocations are page-\/size granularity and page-\/aligned). We think that allocated storage will be suitable for these objects based on the following assumptions\+:


\begin{DoxyEnumerate}
\item 16-\/byte granularity also means 16-\/byte aligned.
\item {\ttfamily new} and other allocators follow the {\ttfamily malloc} rules.
\end{DoxyEnumerate}

We also have some anecdotal evidence\+: we don\textquotesingle{}t see lots of misaligned-\/storage crashes on 32-\/bit i\+OS apps that use {\ttfamily double}.

Apple\textquotesingle{}s allocation reference\+: \href{http://bit.ly/malloc-small}{\texttt{ http\+://bit.\+ly/malloc-\/small}} \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_aa378f7b72cef68ec405b8829e4cc1c90}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!kRegisterPassMaxSize@{kRegisterPassMaxSize}}
\index{kRegisterPassMaxSize@{kRegisterPassMaxSize}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{kRegisterPassMaxSize}{kRegisterPassMaxSize}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_aa378f7b72cef68ec405b8829e4cc1c90} 
std\+::size\+\_\+t kiwi\+::k\+Register\+Pass\+Max\+Size = 16u\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [constexpr]}}

The platform-\/specific maximum size of a value which may be passed by-\/value in registers.

According to each platform ABI, trivially-\/copyable types up to this maximum size may, if the stars align, be passed by-\/value in registers rather than implicitly by-\/reference to stack copies.

Approximate. Accuracy is not promised. \Hypertarget{namespacekiwi_a89fd4d71d71aeb7d7d6e842592e6d652}\index{kiwi@{kiwi}!type\_list\_size\_v@{type\_list\_size\_v}}
\index{type\_list\_size\_v@{type\_list\_size\_v}!kiwi@{kiwi}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{type\_list\_size\_v}{type\_list\_size\_v}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespacekiwi_a89fd4d71d71aeb7d7d6e842592e6d652}

{\bfseries Initial value\+:}
